<span id="freeTextContainer13980217630765807943">An exciting modern day Conan the Barbarian sword & sorcery fantasy, with a dash of V for Vendetta, and an amazingly clever story-within-a-story setup. Stover's construct for wrapping his fantasy world within a dystopian world of science fiction is brilliant, and makes this story memorable as a true hybrid that spans both genres in a holistic way. Beyond that, there's a lot to like here - tons of amusing, vulgarity ridden dialogue and bloody action, and some truly detestable villains that you lov</span>
  <span id="freeText13980217630765807943" style="display:none">An exciting modern day Conan the Barbarian sword &amp; sorcery fantasy, with a dash of V for Vendetta, and an amazingly clever story-within-a-story setup. Stover's construct for wrapping his fantasy world within a dystopian world of science fiction is brilliant, and makes this story memorable as a true hybrid that spans both genres in a holistic way. Beyond that, there's a lot to like here - tons of amusing, vulgarity ridden dialogue and bloody action, and some truly detestable villains that you love to hate. Yet, the story is just too long. Many events are told and then re-told from multiple perspectives. There's too much tangential backstory, and too many twists and turns in the endless plotting and intrigue that obscure the primary plot thread, which is essentially the rescue of a damsel in distress. 30-40% shorter and this could have been perfect.</span>

<div id="review_53460945" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53460945" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/899665-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375036866p2/899665.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53460945?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/899665-jon">Jon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=read-in-my-40s">read-in-my-40s</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53460945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8820025456591684639"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>The pros:</b>
</i> Great combat scenes, lots of fast-paced action, dystopian future Earth reminiscent of ancient history repeating itself, and plots within plots ... all for your entertainment. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>The cons:</b>
</i> Prolific profanity (although I suppose it could be argued that it's all relevant and 'in character'), graphic violence (again relevant and 'in character'), lust/love seen through testosterone-tinged viewpoint and only one decent character afloat in the grey morass of moral ambiguity. <br/><br/><br/><i>Her</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8820025456591684639" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>The pros:</b>
</i> Great combat scenes, lots of fast-paced action, dystopian future Earth reminiscent of ancient history repeating itself, and plots within plots ... all for your entertainment. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>The cons:</b>
</i> Prolific profanity (although I suppose it could be argued that it's all relevant and 'in character'), graphic violence (again relevant and 'in character'), lust/love seen through testosterone-tinged viewpoint and only one decent character afloat in the grey morass of moral ambiguity. <br /><br /><br /><i>Heroes Die</i> drug me through Ankhana at Caine's frenetic pace on his quest to rescue his ex-wife Pallas Rill. On the way, much mayhem, mystery, magic and murder mixed together to clot in a blood-soaked climax spanning two dimensions and leaving the seeds of revolution behind to sprout in both. <br /><br />The beauty and grace of some of the individual combat sequences took my breath away. I re-read some of them just to re-visualize the blow-by-blow more precisely. <br /><br />Oddly, I found myself comparing this story to <i>The Hunger Games</i> from a broader, visionary perspective. Both stories have dystopian totalitarian governments ruling Earth and 'bread and circuses' style entertainment to keep the masses (the workers/castes) in their place. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8820025456591684639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <td colspan="2">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1ebook">1ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=3series">3series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1043833870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1894036013215505639">My first novel by this author & it was quite a pleasant surprise. He handled two distinct worlds very well. One is a high tech, rather dystopian world, the other one full of swords & sorcery. Not a new idea, but it was a rather new way of putting it together with plenty of excitement throughout. <br/><br/>The characters were well drawn with logical, sometimes complex motivations. There were multiple heroic figures, plenty of bad guys, & they didn't always stay where they started out. They grew, diminished</span>
  <span id="freeText1894036013215505639" style="display:none">My first novel by this author &amp; it was quite a pleasant surprise. He handled two distinct worlds very well. One is a high tech, rather dystopian world, the other one full of swords &amp; sorcery. Not a new idea, but it was a rather new way of putting it together with plenty of excitement throughout. <br /><br />The characters were well drawn with logical, sometimes complex motivations. There were multiple heroic figures, plenty of bad guys, &amp; they didn't always stay where they started out. They grew, diminished or died in a complex web.<br /><br />I can definitely see where a second book has a lot of threads that could be spun out, but this one stands well enough on its own. I'm not sure another would be good to read, at least not right away.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1053216223" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2136759505867172931">Middle Earth meets Las Vegas...where lesbian elves pimp hookers and manage casinos, pixy ferries groove as sexy lap warmers, and ogres and trolls are employed as bouncers. HEROES DIE was such a kick in the rumpus! The author has created rich, colorful worlds with strong characters that I loved, loathed, and followed with rapt attention. The protagonist was deadlier than Chuck Norris or Bruce Lee. The female leads were tough, intelligent, and yeah, sexy. I hated to love the evil villain and loved</span>
  <span id="freeText2136759505867172931" style="display:none">Middle Earth meets Las Vegas...where lesbian elves pimp hookers and manage casinos, pixy ferries groove as sexy lap warmers, and ogres and trolls are employed as bouncers. HEROES DIE was such a kick in the rumpus! The author has created rich, colorful worlds with strong characters that I loved, loathed, and followed with rapt attention. The protagonist was deadlier than Chuck Norris or Bruce Lee. The female leads were tough, intelligent, and yeah, sexy. I hated to love the evil villain and loved to hate his henchman. This story would be, should be five stars...but there's one major problem...and its me. I'm just not a fan of the fantasy genre. The dues-ex-machina "magick" is totally abused...winning battles, saving lives, and even elevating mere humans to god-like weapons of mass destruction. However, it's a solid four and one half stars. Highly recommended.</span>

<div id="review_351339166" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351339166" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9774085-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337969621p2/9774085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/351339166?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/9774085-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9774085-sarah?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9774085-sarah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9774085-sarah?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351339166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7717510820707107678">I couldn't finish this one. I renewed it 3 times because I wanted to be able to finish it, but I'm giving up. <br/><br/>This is a fascinating story. The world is interesting, complex and full of potential, as are the male characters. It's well-written and mostly believable. But I'm stuck on two major, major issues.<br/><br/>1) What is with all the shit? And I mean that literally. I'm no wilting lily who can't stand to read about graphic violence, grit and gore. There just seems to be a never-ending river of it in t</span>
  <span id="freeText7717510820707107678" style="display:none">I couldn't finish this one. I renewed it 3 times because I wanted to be able to finish it, but I'm giving up. <br /><br />This is a fascinating story. The world is interesting, complex and full of potential, as are the male characters. It's well-written and mostly believable. But I'm stuck on two major, major issues.<br /><br />1) What is with all the shit? And I mean that literally. I'm no wilting lily who can't stand to read about graphic violence, grit and gore. There just seems to be a never-ending river of it in this book. Again, I mean that literally. At one point the massively injured hero and crew actually swim across a river composed of shit and decomposing bodies. Apparently without increasing the likelihood of their injuries becoming infected. And the mass blood-and-entrails-soaked, naked head-first slide through the hoo-ha of the giant golden hermaphrodite statue of the god/king into the pool of blood (I'm honestly not making this up) was just a little bit over the top. But only a little bit...<br /><br />2) I know that there are male authors out there who can write convincing, realistic female characters. Mr. Stover isn't one of them. Unless there's some radical character development in the last 1/3 of the book, all of the women are stereotypical, 2-dimensional characters. They're also kind of porny, by which I mean their defining characteristic is their sexual objectification. It pisses me off.<br /><br />I want to know how the story ends, but I don't want to jump back into a world that pisses me off and makes me feel like I need to shower. Repeatedly. So, one star for not being able to finish the book, bumped up to two stars because there's so much potential if you can get past the unrealistic portrayal of women...and the shit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7717510820707107678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10708377520089347038">An interesting meld of sf/cyberpunk and fantasy. Exciting and well-plotted.<br/><br/>In a near-future Earth, government control has produced a strict caste society. Hari Michaelson has struggled up from a Labor position, with the help of a rich patron, to become one of the most famous men on Earth - but he is still only an Actor, subservient to those above him. But when he is performing as Caine, sent through a breakthrough in physics to the Otherworld of Ankhana, where elves, ogres, wizards and thieves a</span>
  <span id="freeText10708377520089347038" style="display:none">An interesting meld of sf/cyberpunk and fantasy. Exciting and well-plotted.<br /><br />In a near-future Earth, government control has produced a strict caste society. Hari Michaelson has struggled up from a Labor position, with the help of a rich patron, to become one of the most famous men on Earth - but he is still only an Actor, subservient to those above him. But when he is performing as Caine, sent through a breakthrough in physics to the Otherworld of Ankhana, where elves, ogres, wizards and thieves abound, he can almost be free. And he can take out his aggressions in bloody hand-to-hand combat, murdering for the entertainment of his audience, linked-in to sense his every feeling...<br />But now his estranged wife, also an Actor, is lost in Ankhana, and the time clock is running out before she dies a horrible death. Can Caine succeeed over the political and magickal intrigues of Ankhana, and the even more diabolical plots of his Studio back home, who keep trying to create a more entertaining story, and save the woman he loves?"<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10708377520089347038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180340035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13067644166439557715">So... This book. I'm gonna go with 2.5 stars here. <br/><br/>I started this book a month and a half ago, give or take a couple days. It felt like I was reading it forever and ever... and there were times when I thought it would never end. To be fair, there was a lot going on in my life that made reading take a back-burner, but even when I did pick this book up, it just... didn't grab me. <br/><br/>And in general, I think that's the problem I had overall - I just kept waiting for this book, this story, to grab me...</span>
  <span id="freeText13067644166439557715" style="display:none">So... This book. I'm gonna go with 2.5 stars here. <br /><br />I started this book a month and a half ago, give or take a couple days. It felt like I was reading it forever and ever... and there were times when I thought it would never end. To be fair, there was a lot going on in my life that made reading take a back-burner, but even when I did pick this book up, it just... didn't grab me. <br /><br />And in general, I think that's the problem I had overall - I just kept waiting for this book, this story, to grab me... and it never really did. <br /><br />I never felt any connection with the characters, I never really cared about what happened to them... it was just... a story. A good one - well written and plotted and whatnot, I'll admit that, but from the rave reviews of some of my friends, I expected to pick this book up and be unable to put it back down until it was over. I think my expectations were... pretty high on this one. <br /><br />I just think that maybe this one wasn't for me. Not a bad book, and I'm sure many will love it, but not for me. *shrug* <br /><br />On to the next one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13067644166439557715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3307674332" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3307674332" />
    <a title="Jeremy Jackson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35476632-jeremy-jackson"><img alt="Jeremy Jackson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553798925p2/35476632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3307674332?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeremy Jackson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeremy Jackson" href="/user/show/35476632-jeremy-jackson">Jeremy Jackson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3307674332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5102112598646320934">This is one of the best offerings of old school Grimdark you’ll encounter. <br/>The titular character of the Acts of Caine is a construct; Hari Michaelson is an Actor who is sent to an alternate earth to play a role, enacting adventures to be enjoyed from his own perspective by an eager audience. The lines between Hari and Caine are blurred, but they’re still separate entities, and the way Stover handles it is masterful. The book switches povs, voices, first to third person, fluidly, and the reader h</span>
  <span id="freeText5102112598646320934" style="display:none">This is one of the best offerings of old school Grimdark you’ll encounter. <br />The titular character of the Acts of Caine is a construct; Hari Michaelson is an Actor who is sent to an alternate earth to play a role, enacting adventures to be enjoyed from his own perspective by an eager audience. The lines between Hari and Caine are blurred, but they’re still separate entities, and the way Stover handles it is masterful. The book switches povs, voices, first to third person, fluidly, and the reader has to pay attention to even notice. It’s a well written book, some passages verging on the poetic, and it says something about what it means to be a hero, and who we have to be to claim that title. A fine read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5102112598646320934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6635947-heroes-die">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer530288028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8987519938072533047">I read this book simply to fulfill a reading challenge requirement for one of the Goodreads groups to which I belong. Needless to say, I had zero expectations going in and found myself pretty quickly engrossed in the plot. I'm not even sure quite how to classify this book as it is, in my estimation, equal parts fantasy and science fiction. It's set on Earth albeit many, many, many years in the future when society has evolved (or devolved, depending on the POV) into a caste system and the ideas o</span>
  <span id="freeText8987519938072533047" style="display:none">I read this book simply to fulfill a reading challenge requirement for one of the Goodreads groups to which I belong. Needless to say, I had zero expectations going in and found myself pretty quickly engrossed in the plot. I'm not even sure quite how to classify this book as it is, in my estimation, equal parts fantasy and science fiction. It's set on Earth albeit many, many, many years in the future when society has evolved (or devolved, depending on the POV) into a caste system and the ideas of Abraham Lincoln, John Locke, John Kennedy and others of their ilk are considered grounds for sedition. But it's also set on Overworld, a kingdom closer to a medieval level society that's polpulated by humans and "subs", the substandard species like elves, dwarves, ogres, etc. It's a high octane, action-adventure tale full of violence and greed that nevertheless speaks to the deeper issues of self-identity, what it means to be truly free, and what sorts of evils can arise when society is only willing to consider its own desires. It's a mash-up of The Running Man, The Warriors, Escape From New York, The Truman Show, reality TV, and any sword and sorcery movie you can name. And if all of that sounds crazy that's because it is...and yet, it works. It's an example of old school writing where information and meaning has to be gleaned from the context as there is no spoon feeding done here. But if you pay attention, you'll be rewarded with a fascinating concept and larger than life characters who nevertheless play to motivations that anyone can relate to and recognize. My only quibble? I'm not sure the book needed the epilogue. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8987519938072533047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1418531040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1418531040" />
    <a title="Thomas Stacey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32567361-thomas-stacey"><img alt="Thomas Stacey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460055115p2/32567361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1418531040?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Stacey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Stacey" href="/user/show/32567361-thomas-stacey">Thomas Stacey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1418531040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18116571170739915635">5 testosterone filled blood soaked stars.<br/><br/>This is an incredible book. A seamless blend of sci-fi and fantasy with a genius premise. Set on an overpopulated Earth shackled by a rigid caste society, and set in the land of Ankhana, a distant medieval world where ‘actors’ from Earth are sent to assassinate monarchs, start wars and cause chaos all for the entertainment of billions back home on Earth.<br/><br/>Enter Caine, AKA Hari Michaelson, a superstar actor who’s wife has gone missing in Ankhana. To save her</span>
  <span id="freeText18116571170739915635" style="display:none">5 testosterone filled blood soaked stars.<br /><br />This is an incredible book. A seamless blend of sci-fi and fantasy with a genius premise. Set on an overpopulated Earth shackled by a rigid caste society, and set in the land of Ankhana, a distant medieval world where ‘actors’ from Earth are sent to assassinate monarchs, start wars and cause chaos all for the entertainment of billions back home on Earth.<br /><br />Enter Caine, AKA Hari Michaelson, a superstar actor who’s wife has gone missing in Ankhana. To save her, he must confront the most treacherous rulers of two worlds. Caine is a fascinating character: full of rage and bitterness, he is absolutely relentless and unstoppable - a true anti-hero.<br /><br />This book is an absolute Tour De Force: full of violence, blood and gore. The pace never lets up and you’ll find it extremely difficult to put down, even for essentials such as sleeping or eating. It’s so much more than that though, with a host of intriguing characters to watch develop throughout the story (not always in a good way). Speaking of the story, there’s a lot more going on here than initially appears. To say anything else would be venturing into spoiler territory, but be prepared to be surprised often and without warning. <br /><br />With its slick prose (which reminds me a lot of Scott Lynch), engaging characters and twisting plot, Heroes Die is the book you’ve always needed to read, but never knew it... until now. Read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18116571170739915635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1478898988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8624911184386948113">So there's this very popular actor, - Hari Michaelson - alright? He plays Caine, a fully-fledged badass who kicks all sorts of arse in a fantasy world. Only Ankhana isn't actually a fictitious world, it really exists in a parallel dimension. So, whenever people watch one of Caine's movies, they're watching stuff that's happening for real. <br/><br/>Now Caine... picture a cross between Harry Callahan, Dutch off Predator, John McClane and Conan. That's the sort of badass Caine is. Actually, everybody's a me</span>
  <span id="freeText8624911184386948113" style="display:none">So there's this very popular actor, - Hari Michaelson - alright? He plays Caine, a fully-fledged badass who kicks all sorts of arse in a fantasy world. Only Ankhana isn't actually a fictitious world, it really exists in a parallel dimension. So, whenever people watch one of Caine's movies, they're watching stuff that's happening for real. <br /><br />Now Caine... picture a cross between Harry Callahan, Dutch off Predator, John McClane and Conan. That's the sort of badass Caine is. Actually, everybody's a mean sumbitch in Ankhana: Berne (ah, Berne! Best villain evah!), Ma’elKoth, Majesty... even Pallas Rill, Caine's wife, who needs to be saved.<br /><br />One more thing, I have a major pet peeve: present tense. Whenever I stumble upon a book that's written in present tense, I'll put it down and move on to something else. Well, a considerable chunk of "Heroes Die" is written in present tense. But I'll tell you what? It didn't bother me one bit. Put it this way, it's as if Caine had a gopro strapped on his temple to show us what's going on.<br /><br />Testosterone, people. Plenty of it.<br /><br />Five stars. </span>

As things started to click I got dragged into the story and the end made up for the confusion caused by the beginning.<br/><br/>I still have a bunch of questions about the "setting" that I hope will be answered in the next volume of the series.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uUzpv1ZH8i4o19yG9lZP/ClmW1nZ3hjIqj3PtblTN37oHNCCOBVDYo02cnYN+AQTDBNU8Ii5b1NY0NomKnvSlw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZoG9YHLtCIOasEWKSz4rSNy+46QU2tkbXW6Q7dBtP9830YRdHL+5zz9R63qwkGCn+cvsDUW9roCvg4V+Q0XaNg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer897354576998097327">Matthew Woodring Stover is an American fantasy and science fiction author. He is perhaps best known for his <i>Star Wars</i> novels -- <i>Traitor, Shatterpoint, Revenge of the Sith</i> and <i>Luke Skywalker and the Shadows of Mindor</i>. He has also published several pieces of original work, such as <i>Heroes Die</i>, which Stover described as 'a piece of violent entertainment that is a meditation on violent entertainment'. </span>
  <span id="freeText897354576998097327" style="display:none">Matthew Woodring Stover is an American fantasy and science fiction author. He is perhaps best known for his <i>Star Wars</i> novels -- <i>Traitor, Shatterpoint, Revenge of the Sith</i> and <i>Luke Skywalker and the Shadows of Mindor</i>. He has also published several pieces of original work, such as <i>Heroes Die</i>, which Stover described as 'a piece of violent entertainment that is a meditation on violent entertainment'. Stover's work often emphasises moral ambiguity, psychological verisimilitude and bursts of intense violence. <br /><br />Stover is deeply interested in various forms of martial arts, having trained in the Degerberg Blend, a concept that utilises the thought behind Bruce Lee's Jeet Kune Do as its foundation. </span>
